Complete Definition by Proximate Genus and Differentia
Author defines the complete definition using human as example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the proximate genus and proximate differentia in any given definition and determine whether the definition is complete.

Core Idea
A complete definition requires the proximate genus and proximate differentia; remote genera and differentiae fail to capture the essence.

In logic, a definition must capture the full essence of a thing. The passage uses the example of 'man' to illustrate that a complete definition (الحد التام) must include both the immediate genus (الجنس القريب) and the immediate differentia (الفصل القريب). By understanding which genus and differentia are proximate, you can evaluate whether a definition is complete or deficient. This skill is essential for precise reasoning in Islamic sciences, where definitions underpin legal and theological concepts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Find the definiendum in the passage. The passage defines 'man' (الإنسان), though it is implicitly understood from the context of explaining the complete definition.
The term 'man' is not explicitly stated in the first sentence, but the examples of 'animal', 'rational', etc., make it clear.
2
Extract the proximate genus
Look for the genus that is immediately above the species. The passage states: 'جنسه القريب هو الحيوان' — 'its proximate genus is animal.' This is the category that includes man and other animals.
Remote genera are 'growing' (نام) and 'body' (جسم).
3
Identify the proximate differentia
Find the differentia that separates the species from others under the same proximate genus. The passage says: 'فصله القريب هو (ناطق)' — 'its proximate differentia is rational.' This distinguishes man from other animals.
A remote differentia like 'sentient' (حسّاس) would not fully distinguish man from all animals.
4
Contrast with remote genera and differentiae
Observe how using remote genera or differentiae fails to capture the complete essence. For example, 'growing' includes plants, and 'sentient' includes all animals, so they do not uniquely define man.
The farther the genus, the more general and less specific the definition becomes.
5
Conclude the definition is complete
When both proximate genus and proximate differentia are mentioned, the definition covers all essential properties (ذاتيات) and fully distinguishes the species. This is called a 'hadd tamm' (complete definition).
The passage concludes: 'بذكر الجنس والفصل القريبين يكون التعريف بتمام ماهية الشيء'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العنصر الأول: جنسه القريب، وجنسه القريب هو الحيوان، أما النامي فهو جنس له بعيد وليس بقريب، وأما الجسم فهو جنس له أبعد بدرجتين، وكلما ابتعدنا فإننا نبتعد عن ذكر تمام ذاتياته في حدود هذا العنصر. العنصر الثاني: فصله القريب، وفصله القريب هو (ناطق). وباشتراط الفصل القريب يخرج الفصل البعيد له، كحسّاس، فإن (حسّاس) فصل بعيد للإنسان وليس بقريب، إذ هو فصل لجنسه وهو الحيوان، فإذا ذكر في تعريفه فصله البعيد فإنه لا يميزه عن سائر الحيوانات، وإنما يميزه فقط عن الجماد والنبات، لذلك فلا بد من ذكر فصله القريب، حتى يُميزه تمام تمييز، وبذكر الجنس والفصل القريبين يكون التعريف بتمام ماهية الشيء، أي بتمام ذاتياته.
The first element: its proximate genus, and its proximate genus is 'animal'. As for 'growing', it is a remote genus for it and not proximate. And as for 'body', it is a genus two degrees more remote. The farther we go, the farther we are from mentioning all its essential properties in the definition of this element. The second element: its proximate differentia, and its proximate differentia is 'rational'. By stipulating the proximate differentia, the remote differentia is excluded, like 'sentient', for 'sentient' is a remote differentia for man and not proximate, since it is a differentia for his genus which is animal. So if his remote differentia is mentioned in his definition, it does not distinguish him from the rest of animals, but only distinguishes him from inanimate objects and plants. Therefore, it is necessary to mention his proximate differentia so that he is completely distinguished. By mentioning the proximate genus and differentia, the definition encompasses the complete quiddity of the thing, i.e., all its essential properties.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage explains the components of a complete definition (الحد التام). The author first identifies the proximate genus of man as 'animal' (حيوان). He contrasts it with more remote genera: 'growing' (نام) and 'body' (جسم), noting that the farther the genus, the less it captures the essence. Then he identifies the proximate differentia as 'rational' (ناطق). He explains that using a remote differentia like 'sentient' (حسّاس) would only distinguish man from plants and inanimate objects, not from other animals. Therefore, to fully distinguish man, the proximate differentia is essential. The passage concludes that by mentioning both proximate genus and differentia, the definition covers the complete quiddity (ماهية) or essential properties (ذاتيات). This is a foundational lesson in the theory of definition in logic.

Key Terms
الحد التام (al-ḥadd al-tāmm): A definition that mentions both the proximate genus and the proximate differentia, thereby encompassing the complete essence.
الجنس القريب (al-jins al-qarīb): The immediate genus under which the species falls, e.g., 'animal' for man.
الفصل القريب (al-faṣl al-qarīb): The immediate differentia that distinguishes the species from other species under the same proximate genus, e.g., 'rational' for man.
الماهية (al-māhiyya): The quiddity or essence of a thing, captured by its genus and differentia.

Key Takeaway
A complete definition (الحد التام) must mention both the proximate genus and the proximate differentia to fully capture the essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Expanded vs Concise Definitions of Man
Author provides an expanded phrasing of the complete definition of man.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the genus and differentia in an expanded definition and map them to their concise equivalents.

Core Idea
An expanded definition is just a detailed dress for the genus and differentia.

This passage illustrates how a complete definition can be expressed in a more elaborate form without changing its logical structure. The author defines 'man' with a long phrase, then shows how each part corresponds to the concise terms 'animal' and 'rational'. Understanding this equivalence is key to recognizing valid definitions regardless of wording.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Find the definiendum in the Arabic. In this passage, the term being defined is 'man' (الإنسان).
2
Extract the genus phrase and map to concise genus
The phrase 'body, growing, sentient' (جسم نامٍ حسّاس) is a detailed expression. The author says it is like 'animal' (حيوان) and functions as the proximate genus.
The detailed phrase is logically equivalent to the concise genus.
3
Extract the differentia phrase and map to concise differentia
The phrase 'thinking potentially, apprehending universals and particulars' (متفكر بالقوة مدرك للكليات والجزئيات) is a detailed expression of 'rational' (ناطق) and functions as the proximate differentia.
This shows the differentia can be elaborated without changing its logical role.
4
Confirm definition completeness
Check that the expanded definition includes both genus and differentia. Since both are present and correctly correspond to the concise components, it is a complete definition (hadd haqiqi).
The author's verdict is that it is a valid definition.

B - Like defining man as 'a body, growing, sentient, thinking potentially, apprehending universals and particulars.' So our statement 'body, growing, sentient' is like our statement 'animal', and it is a detailing of it, so it functions as the proximate genus. And our statement 'thinking potentially, apprehending universals and particulars' is an explanation and detailing of the meaning of 'rational' and is similar to it, so it functions as the proximate differentia. Rather, it is in detailed expression.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage gives an example of a complete definition in expanded form. The author defines man as 'a body, growing, sentient, thinking potentially, apprehending universals and particulars.' He then explains that 'body, growing, sentient' is equivalent to the simpler 'animal' — it is a detailed expression that functions as the proximate genus. Similarly, 'thinking potentially, apprehending universals and particulars' is a detailed expression of 'rational' and thus functions as the proximate differentia. This shows that a complete definition can be expressed concisely or with elaboration, as long as the logical components are preserved.

Incomplete Definition and Its Types
Incomplete definition and its types with examples for man

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify an incomplete definition and distinguish it from a complete definition and from rasm.

Core Idea
An incomplete definition still uses essential properties but omits some, like defining man only as 'rational'.

In the previous lesson we learned about complete definitions (الحد التام). Now we turn to incomplete definitions (الحد الناقص), which are also valid definitions but mention only part of the essential properties. The author explains that an incomplete definition can consist of just the proximate differentia, or the differentia with a remote genus. He illustrates with examples for man and then notes a crucial boundary: only composite quiddities can have a hadd (complete or incomplete); simple quiddities must be defined by rasm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and the definition given
In each example, note what is being defined (man) and what expression is used as the definition.
The examples are: 'rational', 'thinking potentially…', 'growing rational', and 'body rational'.
2
Classify the definition by which essential properties are mentioned
Determine whether the definition includes only the differentia, or the differentia together with a genus. If it includes both, check if the genus is remote (e.g., 'body') or less remote ('growing').
'Rational' alone is just the differentia. 'Growing rational' is differentia + a genus (growing), but growing is a remote genus since its genus is body.
3
Compare with a complete definition
Recall that a complete definition of man would be 'rational animal' (proximate genus + differentia). Compare this with the incomplete definitions: they omit either the genus or use a more remote genus.
Incomplete definitions are still definitions, but they do not fully capture the essence.
4
Apply the composite/simple distinction
Note the author's remark: only composite quiddities (like man) can have a hadd. Simple quiddities (e.g., existence, unity) have no genus or differentia and can only be described by rasm.
This is a key boundary in the theory of definition: not every quiddity can be defined by hadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحد الناقص: وهو ما كان تعريفاً للشيء بذكر البعض الذي يفصله عن غيره من ذاتياته .ويكون ذلك بذكر فصله القريب فقط، أو بذكر فصله القريب مع جنسه البعيد، أو بما هو مماثل لذلك. الأمثلة: أ ـ كتعريف الإنسان بأنه (الناطق) أو (المتفكر بالقوة المدرك للكليات والجزئيات). فهذا هو الفصل القريب للإنسان، أو مماثل له وفي قوته كما سبق. ب ـ كتعريف الإنسان بأنه (نام ناطق) أو (جسم ناطق) فهذان تعريفان للإنسان بفصله القريب وجنسه البعيد، إلا أن الجسم جنس أبعد من نام لأنه أعلى منه .ويلاحظ في الحدود أنه لا تحدُ إلا الماهيات المركبة من عنصرين فأكثر، أما البسائط فلا تُعرَّف إلا بالرسم .
Incomplete definition: It is a definition of a thing by mentioning some of its essential properties that distinguish it from others. That can be by mentioning its proximate differentia alone, or by mentioning its proximate differentia together with its remote genus, or by what is equivalent to that. Examples: A - Like defining man as 'the rational' or 'the thinking potentially, apprehending universals and particulars.' That is the proximate differentia of man, or its equivalent and in its power as previously. B - Like defining man as 'growing, rational' or 'body, rational.' These are two definitions of man by his proximate differentia and remote genus, except that 'body' is a more remote genus than 'growing' because it is higher. It is noted in definitions that only composite quiddities (composed of two or more elements) are defined by hadd; as for simple entities, they are only defined by rasm.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage defines the incomplete definition (الحد الناقص). It is a definition that uses only some essential properties, not the full set. The author states that it can be by mentioning only the proximate differentia (e.g., 'rational' for man), or the proximate differentia with a remote genus (e.g., 'growing, rational' or 'body, rational'). Examples are given. Then a note: only composite quiddities (تاهيات مركبة) can be defined by hadd (either complete or incomplete); simple quiddities (بسائط) can only be defined by rasm (description). This is a key distinction in the theory of definition: simple essences have no genus or differentia.

Key Terms
الحد الناقص
الماهيات المركبة
البسائط

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Animal rational
B) Rational

Key Takeaway
An incomplete definition of a composite quiddity mentions only some essential properties, typically the differentia alone or with a remote genus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition of 'wine' (khamr) as 'an intoxicating beverage'. Is this a complete hadd, incomplete hadd, or rasm? Explain which essential properties are mentioned and which are missing. (Complete hadd would include genus 'beverage' and differentia 'intoxicating'; since both are mentioned, it is complete hadd. But if defined as 'intoxicant' alone, that would be incomplete.)
?
In a debate about the definition of 'salah' (prayer), one scholar says 'Salah is the specific actions and words taught by the Prophet.' Another objects that this is a rasm, not a hadd. Using what you learned about incomplete definitions and the composite/simple distinction, explain the objection. (The definition describes the actions/words, which are accidents, not essential properties; therefore it is not a hadd at all, but a rasm.)

Complete Description: Conditions and Invalid Types
Author defines complete description, gives examples and conditions for proper definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a description is a valid complete description and recognize the three types of invalid definitions.

Core Idea
A complete description requires a necessary, comprehensive property, not just any accident.

In this passage, the author defines complete description as a definition by proximate genus and a necessary comprehensive property. He then warns against three common mistakes: using a common accident, a separable property, or a non-comprehensive property. Understanding these conditions helps us evaluate definitions in Islamic sciences like fiqh and kalam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the genus
Find the broader category mentioned in the description. Is it the proximate genus (جنس قريب) that the thing belongs to?
If the genus is too remote, the description may be incomplete.
2
Extract the property
What property follows the genus? Check if it is necessary (لازم) – inseparable from the species – and specific (خاص) – not shared with other species.
Compare with the examples: 'potentially laughing' is necessary; 'actually laughing' is separable.
3
Check comprehensiveness
Does the property apply to all individuals of the species? For example, 'writer' does not apply to all humans, so it fails.
The property must be شامل (comprehensive) in addition to being necessary.
4
Evaluate validity
If any of the three conditions (necessary, specific, comprehensive) is missing, the description is invalid. Use the author's three invalid types as a checklist.
If all conditions are met, the description is a valid complete description (رسم تام).

الرسم التام: هو ما كان تعريفاً للشيء بذكر جنسه القريب مع خاصته اللازمة الشاملة، أي: مع ذكر عرضه اللازم لكل ما صدقاته والخاص به، أو ما هو مماثل لذلك وفي قوته .فلا يصح التعريف بالعرض العام، مثل (الماشي) بالنسبة إلى الإنسان، فهو عرض ليس خاصاً بالإنسان بل هو عام فيه وفي غيره من الحيوانات. ولا يصح التعريف بالخاصة المفارقة غير اللازمة، مثل (الضاحك بالفعل) بالنسبة إلى الإنسان، فالضحك بالفعل من خواص الإنسان المفارقة لا اللازمة، إذ قد يكون بالفعل غير ضاحك بخلاف (الضاحك بالقوة) فهي خاصة لازمة. ولا يصح التعريف بالخاصة غير الشاملة، مثل (الكاتب) بالنسبة إلى الإنسان، وذلك لأن بعض الناس غير كاتب. الأمثلة: أ ـ كتعريف الإنسان بأنه (الحيوان الضاحك بالقوة) أو بأنه (الجسم النامي الحسَّاس الضاحك بالقوة)، فالحيوان ويماثله الجسم النامي الحسَّاس هو الجنس القريب للإنسان، والضاحك بالقوة هو خاصة من خواص الإنسان اللازمة له والشاملة لأفراده. ب ـ كتعريف الحيوان بأنه (نام آكل) فالنامي هو الجنس القريب للحيوان، والآكل هو خاصة من خواصه اللازمة له الشاملة لأفراده.
Complete description: It is a definition of a thing by mentioning its proximate genus together with its necessary comprehensive property, i.e., mentioning its necessary accident that applies to all that it applies to and is specific to it, or what is equivalent to that and in its power. So definition by a common accident is not valid, like 'walker' with respect to man, for it is an accident not specific to man but common to him and other animals. Nor is definition by a separable, non-necessary property valid, like 'actually laughing' with respect to man, for actual laughter is a separable property of man, not necessary, as he may actually not be laughing, unlike 'potentially laughing' which is a necessary property. Nor is definition by a non-comprehensive property valid, like 'writer' with respect to man, because some people are not writers. Examples: A - Like defining man as 'the animal potentially laughing' or as 'the body, growing, sentient, potentially laughing.' So 'animal' and its equivalent 'body, growing, sentient' are the proximate genus of man, and 'potentially laughing' is a property that is necessary for man and comprehensive of his individuals. B - Like defining animal as 'growing, eating.' So 'growing' is the proximate genus of animal, and 'eating' is a property that is necessary for it and comprehensive of its individuals.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage defines the complete description (الرسم التام). It specifies that a complete description consists of the proximate genus plus a necessary and comprehensive property (خاصة لازمة شاملة), i.e., a proper accident that is inseparable from and applies to all individuals of the species. The author then lists three invalid types of definition: (1) using a common accident (عرض عام) that is not specific, e.g., 'walker' for man; (2) using a separable property that is not necessary, e.g., 'actually laughing' because man may not be laughing at all times; (3) using a property that is not comprehensive, e.g., 'writer' because not all men are writers. Valid examples: man as 'animal potentially laughing', and animal as 'growing, eating'. This passage shows that description is an alternative to full definition, especially for simple quiddities or when the differentia is unknown.

الخاصة اللازمة الشاملة
عرض عام
خاصة مفارقة

Key Takeaway
A complete description must combine the proximate genus with a necessary, comprehensive property; using common, separable, or non-comprehensive properties yields an invalid definition.

The Scope of Perfect Definition: Hadd Requires Composition
Author states that hadd is only for composite essences; simples are defined by rasm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine whether a given essence can be defined by hadd or only by rasm based on its composition.

Core Idea
Hadd is only for composite essences; simples must be defined by rasm.

Not every concept can be given a perfect definition (hadd). This lesson explores a key condition: the essence being defined must be composite, composed of genus and differentia. Simple essences, which lack such composition, can only be described (rasm). We will learn to apply this distinction using the example of defining 'man'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum (the thing being defined)
In the passage, the author defines 'man' using two different definitions. Find the term that is being defined: it is 'man' (al-insān).
2
Extract the genus and differentia in each definition
The first definition uses 'growing' (nāmī) as the proximate genus and 'rational' (nāṭiq) as the differentia. The second uses 'body' (jism) as a more remote genus and 'rational' (nāṭiq) as the differentia. Identify which is the genus and which is the differentia in each.
Both are valid hadd definitions because they include a genus and a differentia.
3
Assess the composition of the definiendum
Man is a composite essence because it has both a genus and a differentia. The passage states that only composite essences (murakkaba) can be defined by hadd. Check that the definiendum is indeed composite.
Simple essences like 'existence' (wujūd) have no genus and differentia.
4
Apply the rule: distinguish hadd from rasm
If an essence is composite, it can be defined by hadd (perfect definition). If it is simple, it can only be defined by rasm (description). Use this rule to classify any given definition.
The passage explicitly says 'nothing is defined by a perfect definition except composite essences'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ب ـ وكتعريف الإنسان بأنه (نام ناطق) أو (جسم ناطق) فهذان تعريفان للإنسان بفصله القريب وجنسه البعيد، إلا أن الجسم جنس أبعد من نام لأنه أعلى منه . ويلاحظ في الحدود أنه لا تحدُّ إلا الماهيات المركبة من عنصرين فأكثر، أما البسائط فلا تُعرَّف إلا بالرسم .
B – And like the definition of man as 'rational growing' or 'rational body', these are two definitions of man by its proximate differentia and its remote genus, except that body is a more remote genus than 'growing' because it is higher than it. And it is noted in definitions that nothing is defined by a perfect definition except composite essences consisting of two or more elements; as for simple essences, they are only defined by description.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage discusses the scope of perfect definition (hadd). It first gives an example of defining man with two different definitions: one using 'naamiq natiq' (rational growing) and one using 'jism natiq' (rational body). The author points out that 'body' is a more remote genus than 'growing' because it is higher in the chain of genera. The key point is that perfect definition (hadd) is only applicable to composite essences (mahiyyat murakkaba) that are composed of two or more constituents. Simple essences (basa'it) cannot be defined by hadd; they can only be defined by description (rasm). This distinction is fundamental in logic: hadd requires a genus and differentia, which entails composition, so things that are not composite (like simple concepts or indivisible substances) cannot be given a proper definition but only a descriptive definition. Note that the example with 'naamiq natiq' would be a hadd using a proximate genus (naamiq) and differentia (natiq); the second uses a remote genus (jism). The author uses this example to illustrate that both are definitions of man, but they differ in the genus used.

البسائط

Key Takeaway
Perfect definition (hadd) requires a composite essence; simple essences can only be described (rasm).

Perfect Description (al-Rasm al-Tamm): Conditions and Examples
Author defines rasm tamm and lists invalid types of definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a given description is a valid rasm tamm by checking its two conditions: proximate genus and necessary comprehensive property.

Core Idea
A perfect description uses the proximate genus and a property that is necessary and comprehensive.

In the previous lesson, you learned the difference between hadd (definition) and rasm (description). Now we delve into the perfect description (rasm tamm). The author explains its structure and warns against common mistakes such as using common accidents or separable properties. By understanding these conditions, you will be able to construct sound descriptions in Islamic sciences like fiqh and usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Look for the definiendum in the Arabic. Is it a species like 'man' or 'animal'? This is the subject of the description.
2
Extract the proximate genus
Find the broader category that includes the definiendum. In the example, 'animal' is the proximate genus for 'man'.
If multiple genuses are listed (e.g., 'growing, sensing body'), they are equivalent to 'animal'.
3
Extract the property
Identify the property used alongside the genus. For 'man', it is 'potentially laughing'. This property must be necessary and comprehensive.
4
Test the property for necessity
Ask: Is this property always present in every member of the species? If a man could exist without it, it is not necessary.
Example: 'actually laughing' fails because a man may not be laughing at a given moment.
5
Test the property for comprehensiveness
Ask: Does this property apply to all members of the species? If any individual lacks it, it is not comprehensive.
Example: 'writer' fails because not all men are writers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرسم التام: هو ما كان تعريفاً للشيء بذكر جنسه القريب مع خاصته اللازمة الشاملة، أي: مع ذكر عرضه اللازم لكل ما صدقاته والخاص به، أو ما هو مماثل لذلك وفي قوته . فلا يصح التعريف بالعرض العام، مثل (الماشي) بالنسبة إلى الإنسان، فهو عرض ليس خاصاً بالإنسان بل هو عام فيه وفي غيره من الحيوانات. ولا يصح التعريف بالخاصة المفارقة غير اللازمة، مثل (الضاحك بالفعل) بالنسبة إلى الإنسان، فالضحك بالفعل من خواص الإنسان المفارقة لا اللازمة، إذ قد يكون بالفعل غير ضاحك بخلاف (الضاحك بالقوة) فهي خاصة لازمة. ولا يصح التعريف بالخاصة غير الشاملة، مثل (الكاتب) بالنسبة إلى الإنسان، وذلك لأن بعض الناس غير كاتب . الأمثلة : أ ـ كتعريف الإنسان بأنه (الحيوان الضاحك بالقوة) أو بأنه (الجسم النامي الحسَّاس الضاحك بالقوة)، فالحيوان ويماثله الجسم النامي الحسَّاس هو الجنس القريب للإنسان، والضاحك بالقوة هو خاصة من خواص الإنسان اللازمة له والشاملة لأفراده . ب ـ وكـتـعـريف الحيوان بأنه (نام آكل) فالنامي هو الجنس القريب للحيوان، والآكل هو خاصة من خواصه اللازمة له الشاملة لأفراده .
Perfect description: It is a definition of a thing by mentioning its proximate genus along with its necessary comprehensive property, i.e., mentioning its necessary accident that belongs to everything that falls under it and is specific to it, or something equivalent and having the same force. So definition by a common accident is not valid, such as 'walking' with respect to man, for it is an accident not specific to man but common to him and other animals. And definition by a separable non-necessary property is not valid, such as 'actually laughing' with respect to man, for actual laughing is among the separable properties of man, not necessary, since he may actually not be laughing unlike 'potentially laughing' which is a necessary property. And definition by a non-comprehensive property is not valid, such as 'writer' with respect to man, because some men are not writers. Examples: A – Like the definition of man as 'the animal that potentially laughs' or as 'the growing, sensing body that potentially laughs', for animal and the equivalent growing, sensing body is the proximate genus of man, and potentially laughing is among the necessary properties of man that encompass his individuals. B – And like the definition of animal as 'growing, eating', for 'growing' is the proximate genus of animal, and 'eating' is among its necessary properties that encompass its individuals.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage defines perfect description (rasm tamm). It is a definition that uses the proximate genus (jins qarib) together with a necessary comprehensive property (khassa laazima shaamila). The property must be necessary (i.e., always present) and comprehensive (applying to all members of the species). The author then lists three invalid types of definitions: (1) using a common accident (arad 'amm) like 'walking' for man, which is not exclusive; (2) using a separable non-necessary property (khassa mufariqa ghayr laazima) like 'actually laughing', because someone may not be laughing at the moment; (3) using a non-comprehensive property (khassa ghayr shaamila) like 'writer', because not all men are writers. Then two examples of correct rasm tamm: defining man as 'animal that potentially laughs' (using animal as proximate genus and potential laughter as property), and defining animal as 'growing, eating' (using growing as proximate genus and eating as property). Note that in the second example, 'eating' is a property of animal, though it may seem common to plants? In this context, 'eating' is taken as a property of animals as opposed to plants, which only grow. This demonstrates the logical precision required in constructing definitions.

Key Terms
الرسم التام
الخاصة اللازمة الشاملة
العرض العام
الخاصة المفارقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Man is a featherless biped

Key Takeaway
A perfect description (rasm tamm) requires the proximate genus and a property that is necessary and comprehensive, avoiding common accident, separable property, and non-comprehensive property.

Imperfect Description (Rasm Naqis) and Its Types
Author defines rasm naqis and gives examples with different combinations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four types of imperfect description (rasm naqis) and construct an example of each from Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
A definition can be true without revealing essence — that is rasm naqis.

In the previous lesson, we learned that a perfect description uses the proximate genus and essential differentia. But Islamic logicians recognize that sometimes we cannot or do not need to give the essence. Instead, we can use a set of properties that uniquely identify the thing. This is called imperfect description (rasm naqis). This lesson will break down its four types with examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four types
From the passage, extract the four ways to form a rasm naqis: (i) using only the necessary comprehensive property, (ii) using the property with the remote genus, (iii) using the property with a common accident, (iv) using a set of accidental attributes whose totality is specific.
2
Understand each type with the example of 'man'
For each type, note how the example of man fits: (i) 'potentially laughing' alone, (ii) 'body that potentially laughs' (remote genus + property), (iii) not explicitly given but implied, (iv) 'walking, broad-nailed, bare-skinned, naturally laughing'.
The passage does not explicitly show type (iii), but it is mentioned.
3
Test the condition of totality
For type (iv), check that the set of accidents together are specific to the species. For man, the combination of walking on two feet, broad nails, bare skin, and natural laughter is unique.
4
Apply to an Islamic concept
Choose a concept from fiqh or kalam and try to define it using one of the types of rasm naqis. For example, define 'riba' as 'an increase in a loan without countervalue' (property alone).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرسم الناقص: هو ما كان تعريفاً للشيء بذكر خاصته اللازمة الشاملة، وحدها، أو مع جنسه البعيد، أو مع عرضه العام، أو بذكر عرضيات له تختص جملتها بحقيقته . الأمثلة : أ ـ كتعريف الإنسان بأنه الضاحك بالقوة) أو (القابل للعلم وصنعة الكتابة فكل منها بالنسبة إلى الإنسان من خواصه اللازمة الشاملة لكل أفراده . ب ـ وكتعريف الإنسان بأنه جسم ضاحك بالقوة) فالجسم جنس بعيد للإنسان، وضاحك بالقوة خاصة لازمة شاملة من خواصه . جـ ـ وكتعريف الإنسان بأنه ماش على قدميه عريض الأظفار بادي البشرة ضحاك بالطبع فكل هذه عرضيات تختص جملتها بحقيقة نوع الإنسان .
Imperfect description: It is a definition of a thing by mentioning its necessary comprehensive property alone, or with its remote genus, or with its common accident, or by mentioning accidental attributes of it whose totality is specific to its reality. Examples: A – Like the definition of man as 'potentially laughing' or 'capable of knowledge and the craft of writing', for each of these is among his necessary comprehensive properties encompassing all his individuals. B – And like the definition of man as 'a body that potentially laughs', for body is a remote genus of man, and 'potentially laughing' is a necessary comprehensive property among his properties. C – And like the definition of man as 'walking on two feet, broad-nailed, bare-skinned, naturally laughing', for all these are accidental attributes whose totality is specific to the reality of the human species.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage defines imperfect description (rasm naqis). Unlike perfect description which requires proximate genus, rasm naqis can be formed in several ways: (i) using only the necessary comprehensive property (e.g., 'man is potentially laughing'); (ii) using the property together with the remote genus (e.g., 'man is a body that potentially laughs'); (iii) using the property with a common accident; (iv) using a set of accidental attributes that together are unique to the species (e.g., 'man is a walking, broad-nailed, bare-skinned, naturally laughing being'). The examples illustrate these types. In example A, the property alone is sufficient: 'potentially laughing' and 'capable of knowledge and writing' are both necessary comprehensive properties. In example B, it uses the remote genus 'body' with the property. In example C, it lists several accidents that collectively distinguish man from other animals. This shows that a description can be imperfect in the sense that it does not give the essence, but still identifies the thing uniquely.

الرسم الناقص
الجنس البعيد
خاصة لازمة
عرض عام

Key Takeaway
Imperfect description (rasm naqis) identifies a thing by its necessary properties or a unique combination of accidents, without stating its essence.

Understanding Verbal Definition (al-Ta'rif al-Lafzi)
Author defines verbal definition as using a synonymous term known to the listener.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a verbal definition and explain why a synonym is considered a property of the thing.

Core Idea
Verbal definition explains an unfamiliar word by a known synonym.

In Islamic logic, definitions come in various forms. One straightforward type is the verbal definition (al-ta'rif al-lafzi), where an unknown word is clarified by a synonym known to the hearer. This passage defines the concept and provides three illustrative examples, including the definition of 'al-qaswara' as 'al-asad' (lion). Understanding this tool helps you see how scholars clarify terms in disciplines like Tafsir and Fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of verbal definition.
The author defines it as explaining a word with a synonymous word known to the addressee. Notice the condition of being 'known'.
2
Understand the synonym as a property.
The author notes that the synonym is in reality a property of the thing. This relates to the theory of properties in logic: a synonym shares the same meaning, so it is a property of the word.
3
Examine each example to verify it fits.
For (a) al-birr as al-qamh, (b) al-qaswara as al-asad, and (c) al-qar' as ambiguous between menstruation and purity. Check that each uses a known synonym (or in (c) lists meanings).
The third example is slightly different as it clarifies by mentioning the multiple meanings, not a single synonym.
4
Apply the concept to recognizing verbal definitions elsewhere.
Now you can identify verbal definitions in Islamic texts: when an author says 'X means Y' where Y is a synonym, that is a verbal definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التعريف اللفظي : وهو تعريف اللفظ بلفظ آخر مرادف له معلوم عند المخاطب، ومرادف الشيء هو في الحقيقة خاصة من خواصه . الأمثلة : أ ـ كتعريف البر بأنه (القمح). ب ـ وكتعريف القسورة بأنه (الأسد). جـ ـ وكتعريف القرء بأنه لفظ مشترك بين الحيض والطهر .
Verbal definition: It is the definition of a word by another word that is synonymous with it and known to the addressee, and the synonym of a thing is in reality one of its properties. Examples: A – Like the definition of 'al-birr' as 'al-qamh' (wheat). B – And like the definition of 'al-qaswara' as 'al-asad' (lion). C – And like the definition of 'al-qar'' as a word shared between menstruation and purity (i.e., ambiguous).
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage defines verbal definition (ta'rif lafzi). It is a definition that explains an unfamiliar word by using a synonym that the listener knows. The author notes that a synonym is actually a property of the thing being defined. Three examples are given: (a) defining 'al-birr' (which can mean wheat or piety) as 'al-qamh' (wheat) — here the synonym clarifies the specific meaning; (b) defining 'al-qaswara' as 'al-asad' (lion) — 'qaswara' is a less common word for lion; (c) defining 'al-qar'' as a word that is shared (mushtarak) between menstruation and purity — this is actually a definition of a ambiguous term by listing its meanings, not a simple synonym. The third example illustrates that sometimes a verbal definition may involve multiple possible meanings. This type of definition is essential in linguistics and jurisprudence for clarifying ambiguous terms.

Key Terms
التعريف اللفظي
المرادف

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Defining 'al-qaswara' as 'al-asad'

D) Defining 'heat' as molecular motion

Key Takeaway
Verbal definition is a simple yet essential tool in the Islamic sciences for clarifying words by known synonyms.

Definition by Example in Logic
Author defines definition by example and gives examples from grammar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a definition by example and explain its function using examples from Arabic grammar.

Core Idea
Definition by example teaches through representative instances, not formal categories.

Sometimes the clearest way to define a concept is to give an example that embodies it. In this passage, the author introduces definition by example (al-ta'rif bi'l-mithal) and illustrates it with grammatical rules for noun and verb. This tool is powerful for conveying abstract categories through concrete models.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concept being defined
Locate the term 'التعريف بالمثال' (definition by example) in the Arabic. The author tells you exactly what is being defined: a method of definition.
2
Extract the method's description
Read the explanation: 'وهو تعريف الشيء بذكر مثال من أمثلته' – it means defining a thing by mentioning one of its examples. Note that the example is considered a property (خاصة) of the thing.
This shows that definition by example relies on a characteristic instance.
3
Analyze the grammatical examples
The author gives two examples from Arabic grammar: (a) defining a noun by saying it resembles the words 'Zayd', 'rajul', and 'alladhi'; (b) defining a verb by saying it resembles 'sami'a', 'yaqul', and 'khudh'. Observe how these examples cover the main types of each part of speech.
The examples serve as templates: any word that behaves like these is a noun or verb.
4
Assess the usefulness of this method
Consider why definition by example is helpful: when a precise definition is difficult, examples give the learner a pattern to recognize other instances. It is a pedagogical shortcut.
In logic, this is accepted as a valid type of description (rasm), especially for beginners.

التعريف بالمثال : وهو تعريف الشيء بذكر مثال من أمثلته، ومثال الشيء هو في الحقيقة خاصة من خواصه . الأمثلة : أ ـ كتعريف الاسم بأنه ما أشبه لفظ زيد ورجل والذي . ب ـ وكتعريف الفعل بأنه ما أشبه لفظ سَمِعَ ويقول وخُذْ .
Definition by example: It is the definition of a thing by mentioning an example of its examples, and the example of a thing is in reality one of its properties. Examples: A – Like the definition of noun (ism) as 'what resembles the word Zayd, rajul, and alladhi'. B – And like the definition of verb (fi'l) as 'what resembles the word sami'a, yaqul, and khudh'.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage defines definition by example (ta'rif bi'l-mithal). It explains a concept by giving a specific instance that serves as a model. The example is considered a property of the thing being defined. Two examples are from Arabic grammar: (a) defining a noun (ism) by saying it is like 'Zayd' (a proper noun), 'rajul' (a common noun), and 'alladhi' (a relative pronoun) — these are examples of words that are nouns; (b) defining a verb (fi'l) by saying it is like 'sami'a' (past tense), 'yaqul' (present tense), and 'khudh' (imperative). This method is especially useful when a precise definition is difficult, and the examples give the listener a pattern to identify other instances. In logic, this is a common pedagogical tool.

Definition by Division: Meaning and Conditions
Author begins definition of definition by division with its basic meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define definition by division and identify the conditions that make it a valid logical definition.

Core Idea
Definition by division explains a concept by enumerating its exclusive parts.

In this lesson, we explore the logical method known as definition by division (al-ta'rif bi'l-taqsim). The Arabic passage introduces its basic meaning: defining something by mentioning the divisions into which it falls. However, for this method to be valid, the division must be exhaustive and mutually exclusive—conditions the author likely expands on later. We will unpack this definition and see how it applies in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Locate the term being defined. In this passage, it is 'definition by division' (al-ta'rif bi'l-taqsim).
The definiendum is a logical method, not an object.
2
Extract the genus and differentia
The genus is 'definition' (ta'rif). The differentia is 'by mentioning divisions' (bi-dhikr al-aqsam). So it is a type of definition that uses division.
The genus tells us it is a definition; the differentia tells us how.
3
Consider the missing conditions
A valid division must be exhaustive (cover all types) and exclusive (no overlap). The passage does not mention these, but they are required for a proper definition by division.
For example, dividing 'knowledge' into 'tasawwur' and 'tasdiq' is exhaustive and exclusive only if these two categories cover all knowledge without overlap.

Definition by division: It is the definition of a thing by mentioning the divisions into which it is divided.

Commentary
This passage introduces definition by division (ta'rif bi'l-taqsim). It defines it as explaining a thing by listing the categories or parts into which it is divided. For example, defining 'knowledge' by saying it is divided into tasawwur (conception) and tasdiq (assent). Unfortunately, the text here is cut off at page 70, so we do not have the examples that would typically follow. However, the meaning is clear: this type of definition uses division as a way to clarify the extent of a concept. In logic, division must be exhaustive and mutually exclusive to be a proper definition. This method is common in books on logic when classifying concepts.

Types of Incomplete and Other Definitions
Author defines and exemplifies four types of non-hadd definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish between incomplete definition (rasm), verbal definition, definition by example, and definition by division in Islamic logical texts.

Core Idea
Incomplete definitions combine properties to describe essence without reaching a complete definition (hadd).

This passage classifies definitions beyond the complete definition (hadd). The author explains four types: incomplete definition, verbal definition, definition by example, and definition by division. Understanding these helps you evaluate how definitions function in Islamic sciences, from fiqh to grammar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of definition
Read the definition and determine which of the four types it belongs to: incomplete (rasm), verbal (lafzi), by example (mithal), or by division (taqsim).
Look for key indicators: synonym for verbal, instance for example, enumeration of parts for division.
2
Extract the components
For an incomplete definition, identify whether it uses a specific property alone, or with a remote genus, general accident, or a set of accidental properties.
The passage gives examples for man: khassa alone, khassa + remote genus, etc.
3
Compare strength of combinations
The author states that definitions with multiple components are stronger. Note which combinations are more complete.
General observations 1–4 rank combinations like differentia + specific property as stronger than differentia alone.
4
Assess whether it is a hadd or rasm
Determine if the definition gives the complete essence (hadd) or merely describes (rasm). The passage focuses on incomplete (rasm) definitions.
Incomplete definitions lack the full genus and differentia that constitute a hadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرسم الناقص: هو ما كان تعريفاً للشيء بذكر خاصته اللازمة الشاملة، وحدها، أو مع جنسه البعيد، أو مع عرضه العام، أو بذكر عرضيات له تختص جملتها بحقيقته .
الأمثلة :
أ ـ كتعريف الإنسان بأنه الضاحك بالقوة) أو (القابل للعلم وصنعة الكتابة فكل منها بالنسبة إلى الإنسان من خواصه اللازمة الشاملة لكل أفراده .
ب ـ وكتعريف الإنسان بأنه جسم ضاحك بالقوة) فالجسم جنس بعيد للإنسان، وضاحك بالقوة خاصة لازمة شاملة من خواصه .
جـ ـ وكتعريف الإنسان بأنه ماش على قدميه عريض الأظفار بادي البشرة ضحاك بالطبع فكل هذه عرضيات تختص جملتها بحقيقة نوع الإنسان .
التعريف اللفظي : وهو تعريف اللفظ بلفظ آخر مرادف له معلوم عند المخاطب، ومرادف الشيء هو في الحقيقة خاصة من خواصه .
الأمثلة :
أ ـ كتعريف البر بأنه (القمح).
ب ـ وكتعريف القسورة بأنه (الأسد).
جـ ـ وكتعريف القرء بأنه لفظ مشترك بين الحيض والطهر .
التعريف بالمثال : وهو تعريف الشيء بذكر مثال من أمثلته، ومثال الشيء هو في الحقيقة خاصة من خواصه .
الأمثلة :
أ ـ كتعريف الاسم بأنه ما أشبه لفظ زيد ورجل والذي .
ب ـ وكتعريف الفعل بأنه ما أشبه لفظ سَمِعَ ويقول وخُذْ .
التعريف بالتقسيم : وهو تعريف الشيء بذكر الأقسام التي ينقسم إليها، ومعلوم أن أقسام الشيء خاصةٌ من خواصه.
الأمثلة :
أ ـ كتعريف الكلمة بأنها اسم وفعل وحرف.
ب ـ وكتعريف العدد بأنه زوج وفرد.
ملاحظات عامة :
١ ـ التعريف المركب من العرض العام والفصل أقوى مما فيه الفصل وحده .
٢ ـ التعريف المركب من الجنس البعيد والفصل أقوى مما فيه الفصل وحده .
٣ ـ التعريف المركب من الفصل والخاصة أكمل وأقوى من المركب من الفصل والعرض العام.
٤ ـ التعريف المركب من العرض العام والخاصة أقوى مما فيه الخاصة وحدها .
وكل تعريف فيه زيادة بيان للمفرد المشروح هو أقوى وأكمل مما ليس فيه هذه الزيادة .
٥ ـ تعاريف الألفاظ تقوم مقامها إذا كانت تعاريف كاملة صحيحة، فلو وُضِع بدل الجنس حدُّه لكفى، ولو وُضِع بدلَ الفصل حدُّه لكفى، ولو وضع بدل الخاصة حدُّها لكفى .
٦ ـ عناية المنطقي بالمعاني، وأما الألفاظ فهي قوالب لها، ودالاتٌ عليها .
The incomplete definition (al-rasm al-naqis): It is what constitutes a definition of a thing by mentioning its inseparable comprehensive specific property (khassa) alone, or together with its remote genus, or together with its general accident, or by mentioning accidental properties of it whose totality is specific to its reality. Examples: (a) Such as defining man as 'potentially laughing' or 'capable of knowledge and the craft of writing', for each of these is, with respect to man, among his inseparable comprehensive specific properties covering all his individuals. (b) And such as defining man as 'a body potentially laughing' — 'body' is a remote genus for man, and 'potentially laughing' is an inseparable comprehensive specific property among his properties. (c) And such as defining man as 'walking on two feet, broad-nailed, bare-skinned, naturally laughing' — all these are accidental properties whose totality is specific to the reality of the human species. The verbal definition (al-ta'rif al-lafzi): It is defining a word by another synonymous word known to the addressee, and the synonym of a thing is in reality one of its specific properties. Examples: (a) Such as defining 'al-birr' as 'wheat'. (b) And such as defining 'al-qaswara' as 'lion'. (c) And such as defining 'al-qur'' as a word shared between menstruation and purity. The definition by example (al-ta'rif bi al-mithal): It is defining a thing by mentioning an example from its instances, and the example of a thing is in reality one of its specific properties. Examples: (a) Such as defining the noun as 'whatever resembles the word Zaid, rajul, and alladhi'. (b) And such as defining the verb as 'whatever resembles the word sami'a, yaqulu, and khudh'. The definition by division (al-ta'rif bi al-taqsim): It is defining a thing by mentioning the divisions into which it is divided, and it is known that the divisions of a thing are among its specific properties. Examples: (a) Such as defining the word (kalima) as 'noun, verb, and particle'. (b) And such as defining number as 'even and odd'. General observations: 1. A definition composed of a general accident and a differentia is stronger than one containing the differentia alone. 2. A definition composed of a remote genus and a differentia is stronger than one containing the differentia alone. 3. A definition composed of a differentia and a specific property is more complete and stronger than one composed of a differentia and a general accident. 4. A definition composed of a general accident and a specific property is stronger than one containing the specific property alone. And every definition in which there is an increase in clarification of the explained term is stronger and more complete than one lacking this increase. 5. Verbal definitions stand in place of the defined terms if they are complete and correct definitions. So if one substitutes for a genus its own definition (hadd), it suffices; if one substitutes for a differentia its own definition, it suffices; if one substitutes for a specific property its own definition, it suffices. 6. The logician's concern is with meanings, while words are their moulds and indicators of them.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a classification and explanation of types of definitions, specifically incomplete definitions (rasm), verbal definitions, definitions by example, and definitions by division, followed by general observations about the strength of combinations of definitional components. The author begins with the incomplete definition (al-rasm al-naqis), which defines a thing by mentioning its inseparable comprehensive specific property (khassa) either alone, or with its remote genus, or with its general accident, or by a collection of accidental properties that together are specific to the thing's essence. Three examples are given for man: (a) 'potentially laughing' or 'capable of knowledge and writing'—each is an inseparable specific property covering all humans; (b) 'a body potentially laughing' where 'body' is a remote genus and 'potentially laughing' is a specific property; (c) 'walking on two feet, broad-nailed, bare-skinned, naturally laughing'—a set of accidental properties that collectively distinguish humans. Next, the author defines verbal definition (al-ta'rif al-lafzi) as defining a word by a synonym known to the listener, noting that a synonym is in reality one of the thing's specific properties. Examples: defining 'al-birr' (commonly meaning 'righteousness' but here referring to 'wheat') as 'wheat'; defining 'al-qaswara' as 'lion'; and defining 'al-qur'' as a homonym for menstruation and purity. Then definition by example (al-ta'rif bi al-mithal) is introduced: defining a thing by giving one of its instances, which also is a specific property. Examples: defining the noun by resemblance to 'Zaid', 'rajul', and 'alladhi'; defining the verb by resemblance to 'sami'a', 'yaqulu', and 'khudh'. Finally, definition by division (al-ta'rif bi al-taqsim) divides the thing into its parts, which are also specific properties. Examples: defining 'kalima' (word) as noun, verb, and particle; defining number as even and odd. The passage concludes with six general observations: (1-4) Combinations of components like general accident + differentia, remote genus + differentia, differentia + specific property, and general accident + specific property are stronger (i.e., more informative) than the components alone. (5) Verbal definitions can replace the defined term if they are complete and correct; substituting a genus with its own definition suffices, similarly for differentia and specific property. (6) The logician focuses on meanings, while words are merely tools and indicators. This passage teaches that definitions can take various forms, but the most informative combine multiple components.

Key Terms
الرسم الناقص (al-rasm al-naqis): An incomplete definition that mentions a specific property (alone or with other components) but does not give the complete essence (hadd). [Note: In later works, the term rasm is sometimes used more broadly; here it specifically contrasts with hadd.]
الخاصة اللازمة الشاملة (al-khassa al-lazima al-shamila): An inseparable specific property that applies to all individuals of a species, e.g., 'potentially laughing' for humans.
الجنس البعيد (al-jins al-ba'id): The remote genus, a higher genus not immediately above the species, e.g., 'body' for human.
العرض العام (al-'arad al-'amm): A general accident that applies to multiple species, not specific to one.
التعريف اللفظي (al-ta'rif al-lafzi): Defining a word by a synonym known to the listener; essentially a verbal substitution.
التعريف بالمثال (al-ta'rif bi al-mithal): Defining a thing by giving an example from its instances.
التعريف بالتقسيم (al-ta'rif bi al-taqsim): Defining a thing by enumerating its divisions or parts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Defining man as 'potentially laughing'.
C) Defining number as 'even and odd'.
D) Defining the noun as 'what resembles Zaid and rajul'.

Key Takeaway
Incomplete definitions and verbal definitions are essential tools in Islamic logic for clarifying concepts without requiring a full essential definition.

Divisions as Properties
Author states that divisions of a thing are among its properties.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify an exhaustive division as a property (khassa) of a thing and provide examples from Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
Every exhaustive division of a thing is a property that fully differentiates it.

In logic, definitions can be composed of various components. One important insight is that the divisions of a thing—breaking it into its exhaustive parts—constitute a property (khassa). This lesson explores that idea through examples of word and number.

Guided Path
1
Understand the claim
The author states that divisions of a thing are among its properties. This means that listing the exhaustive parts of something can serve as a definition by distinguishing it from others.
A property is a non-essential accident that is co-extensive with the thing.
2
Consider the example of 'word'
In Arabic grammar, a word (kalima) is divided into noun, verb, and particle. This division is exhaustive and unique to words, so it is a property.
This is the standard definition of kalima in nahw.
3
Consider the example of 'number'
Number is divided into even and odd. This division exhausts all numbers and is unique to them, forming a property.
Even and odd are mutually exclusive and collectively exhaustive.
4
Apply the concept
Think of other Islamic science concepts that can be defined by their divisions, e.g., 'ruling' (hukm) in usul al-fiqh divided into taklifi and wadi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومعلوم أن أقسام الشيء خاصةٌ من خواصه.
الأمثلة:
أ ـ كتعريف الكلمة بأنها اسم وفعل وحرف.
ب ـ وكتعريف العدد بأنه زوج وفرد.
ملاحظات عامة:
١ ـ التعريف المركب من العرض العام والفصل أقوى مما فيه الفصل وحده.
٢ ـ التعريف المركب من الجنس البعيد والفصل أقوى مما فيه الفصل وحده.
٣ ـ التعريف المركب من الفصل والخاصة أكمل وأقوى من المركب من الفصل والعرض العام.
٤ ـ التعريف المركب من العرض العام والخاصة أقوى مما فيه الخاصة وحدها.
وكل تعريف فيه زيادة بيان للمفرد المشروح هو أقوى وأكمل مما ليس فيه هذه الزيادة.
٥ ـ تعاريف الألفاظ تقوم مقامها إذا كانت تعاريف كاملة صحيحة، فلو وُضِع بدل الجنس حدُّه لكفى، ولو وُضِع بدلَ الفصل حدُّه لكفى، ولو وضع بدل الخاصة حدُّها لكفى.
٦ ـ عناية المنطقي بالمعاني، وأما الألفاظ فهي قوالب لها، ودالاتٌ عليها.
And it is known that the divisions of a thing are among its properties.
Examples:
a) Like defining 'word' (kalima) as noun, verb, and particle.
b) Like defining 'number' as even and odd.
General notes:
1. A definition composed of common accident and differentia is stronger than one containing only the differentia.
2. A definition composed of remote genus and differentia is stronger than one containing only the differentia.
3. A definition composed of differentia and property is more perfect and stronger than one composed of differentia and common accident.
4. A definition composed of common accident and property is stronger than one containing only the property.
And every definition that adds explanation of the explained term is stronger and more perfect than that which lacks this addition.
5. Definitions of words take their place if they are complete and correct definitions: if the definition of the genus is substituted for the genus, it suffices; if the definition of the differentia is substituted for the differentia, it suffices; if the definition of the property is substituted for the property, it suffices.
6. The logician's concern is with meanings; words are merely their molds and indicators of them.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage discusses the various types of definitions in logic and ranks them by strength. The author begins by stating that the divisions (aqsam) of a thing are among its properties (khawas). This is because any exhaustive division, such as dividing 'word' into noun, verb, and particle, or 'number' into even and odd, constitutes a property (khassa) of that thing. Then the author gives general observations on comparative strength of composite definitions. A definition combining a common accident ('arad 'amm) with a differentia (fasl) is stronger than one with only the differentia. Similarly, combining a remote genus (jins ba'id) with a differentia is stronger than the differentia alone. Combining a differentia with a property (khassa) is more perfect than combining differentia with common accident, because the property co-extends with the thing. Combining common accident with property is stronger than property alone. The principle is that more explanatory components yield stronger definitions. The author then notes that if the definitions of the terms used (genus, differentia, property) are themselves correct, they can replace those terms in a definition. Finally, a crucial meta-note: logic is concerned with meanings (ma'ani), not words (alfaz); words are merely vehicles. This guards against confusing verbal disputes with logical analysis.

Key Terms
خاصة (khassa): A property (khassa) is a non-essential accident that is co-extensive with the thing; here, the divisions of a thing are counted as among its properties. [Note: Stable term across logical works; sometimes distinguished from 'arad 'amm as more specific.]
عرض عام ('arad 'amm): A common accident is an accident that is not co-extensive with the thing, e.g., 'being divisible' for numbers (both even and odd share it). [Note: No significant shift.]
فصل (fasl): Differentia is the essential part of the definition that distinguishes a species from its co-generic species. [Note: Stable across Mantiq tradition.]
جنس بعيد (jins ba'id): Remote genus is a higher genus in the tree, not the immediate genus of the species. [Note: Notion of 'remote' vs 'near' standard.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) its differentia

Key Takeaway
The divisions of a thing, when exhaustive, constitute a property that can serve as a definition.

Ranking Composite Definitions
Author enumerates rankings of composite definitions and a substitution rule.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to rank various composite definitions by strength based on the components used and explain why more explanatory components yield stronger definitions.

Core Idea
Composite definitions are stronger than single-component definitions, and more explanation means stronger definition.

Not all definitions are equal. The author provides a hierarchy of composite definitions based on which of the five universals they combine. This lesson dissects each ranking and the underlying principle that more explanation yields a stronger definition.

Guided Path
1
List the comparisons
The author gives four pairwise strength comparisons: (a) common accident+differentia > differentia alone; (b) remote genus+differentia > differentia alone; (c) differentia+property > differentia+common accident; (d) common accident+property > property alone. Write them down.
Pay attention to the 'stronger' (أقوى) and 'more perfect' (أكمل) language.
2
Identify the pattern
The stronger definition has more components (except when comparing like with like). The principle: 'more explanation' (زيادة بيان) strengthens the definition.
The author states: 'كل تعريف فيه زيادة بيان للمفرد المشروح هو أقوى وأكمل'.
3
Understand the substitution rule
If the components themselves have correct definitions, they can be replaced by those definitions without loss. This allows building definitions from simpler ones.
This applies to genus, differentia, and property.
4
Apply to an Islamic example
Consider defining 'salah' (prayer) as a composite: remote genus (act of worship), differentia (with specific actions), property (includes bowing and prostrating). How would this rank against a simpler definition?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومعلوم أن أقسام الشيء خاصةٌ من خواصه.
الأمثلة:
أ ـ كتعريف الكلمة بأنها اسم وفعل وحرف.
ب ـ وكتعريف العدد بأنه زوج وفرد.
ملاحظات عامة:
١ ـ التعريف المركب من العرض العام والفصل أقوى مما فيه الفصل وحده.
٢ ـ التعريف المركب من الجنس البعيد والفصل أقوى مما فيه الفصل وحده.
٣ ـ التعريف المركب من الفصل والخاصة أكمل وأقوى من المركب من الفصل والعرض العام.
٤ ـ التعريف المركب من العرض العام والخاصة أقوى مما فيه الخاصة وحدها.
وكل تعريف فيه زيادة بيان للمفرد المشروح هو أقوى وأكمل مما ليس فيه هذه الزيادة.
٥ ـ تعاريف الألفاظ تقوم مقامها إذا كانت تعاريف كاملة صحيحة، فلو وُضِع بدل الجنس حدُّه لكفى، ولو وُضِع بدلَ الفصل حدُّه لكفى، ولو وضع بدل الخاصة حدُّها لكفى.
٦ ـ عناية المنطقي بالمعاني، وأما الألفاظ فهي قوالب لها، ودالاتٌ عليها.
And it is known that the divisions of a thing are among its properties.
Examples:
a) Like defining 'word' (kalima) as noun, verb, and particle.
b) Like defining 'number' as even and odd.
General notes:
1. A definition composed of common accident and differentia is stronger than one containing only the differentia.
2. A definition composed of remote genus and differentia is stronger than one containing only the differentia.
3. A definition composed of differentia and property is more perfect and stronger than one composed of differentia and common accident.
4. A definition composed of common accident and property is stronger than one containing only the property.
And every definition that adds explanation of the explained term is stronger and more perfect than that which lacks this addition.
5. Definitions of words take their place if they are complete and correct definitions: if the definition of the genus is substituted for the genus, it suffices; if the definition of the differentia is substituted for the differentia, it suffices; if the definition of the property is substituted for the property, it suffices.
6. The logician's concern is with meanings; words are merely their molds and indicators of them.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage discusses the various types of definitions in logic and ranks them by strength. The author begins by stating that the divisions (aqsam) of a thing are among its properties (khawas). This is because any exhaustive division, such as dividing 'word' into noun, verb, and particle, or 'number' into even and odd, constitutes a property (khassa) of that thing. Then the author gives general observations on comparative strength of composite definitions. A definition combining a common accident ('arad 'amm) with a differentia (fasl) is stronger than one with only the differentia. Similarly, combining a remote genus (jins ba'id) with a differentia is stronger than the differentia alone. Combining a differentia with a property (khassa) is more perfect than combining differentia with common accident, because the property co-extends with the thing. Combining common accident with property is stronger than property alone. The principle is that more explanatory components yield stronger definitions. The author then notes that if the definitions of the terms used (genus, differentia, property) are themselves correct, they can replace those terms in a definition. Finally, a crucial meta-note: logic is concerned with meanings (ma'ani), not words (alfaz); words are merely vehicles. This guards against confusing verbal disputes with logical analysis.

Key Terms
خاصة (khassa): A property (khassa) is a non-essential accident that is co-extensive with the thing; here, the divisions of a thing are counted as among its properties. [Note: Stable term across logical works; sometimes distinguished from 'arad 'amm as more specific.]
عرض عام ('arad 'amm): A common accident is an accident that is not co-extensive with the thing, e.g., 'being divisible' for numbers (both even and odd share it). [Note: No significant shift.]
فصل (fasl): Differentia is the essential part of the definition that distinguishes a species from its co-generic species. [Note: Stable across Mantiq tradition.]
جنس بعيد (jins ba'id): Remote genus is a higher genus in the tree, not the immediate genus of the species. [Note: Notion of 'remote' vs 'near' standard.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) differentia alone
B) differentia and common accident
C) property alone
D) remote genus and differentia

Key Takeaway
Composite definitions increase in strength with the number of explanatory components, and substitution of components with their definitions is permissible if correct.

Defining the Categorical Proposition
Author defines the categorical proposition as a judgment of attribution or negation between two terms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the defining features of a categorical proposition and distinguish it from other proposition types.

Core Idea
A categorical proposition is a simple attribution or negation between two terms, nothing more.

In this passage, the author distills the essence of the categorical proposition from the earlier discussion on propositions. Two equivalent formulations are given, each emphasizing that the judgment is direct and unconditional. Understanding this definition is the foundation for all syllogistic reasoning in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definiendum
Find the term being defined in the Arabic: 'القضية الحملية' (categorical proposition). Note that the author is providing a definition extracted from the previous discussion.
2
Extract the two equivalent definitions
The author gives two formulations. First: the judgment is based on attributing something to something else or negating it. Second: the judgment is a positive or negative relation between a subject (مسند إليه) and a predicate (مسند). Both say the same thing in different words.
The first uses 'إسناد', the second uses 'علاقة موجبة أو سالبة'.
3
Compare with conditional propositions
Contrast this definition with that of a conditional proposition (القضية الشرطية), which connects two propositions (e.g., 'If ... then ...'). The categorical proposition stands alone; it does not depend on another proposition.
This helps clarify why it is called 'hamliyya' (attributive).
4
Identify the key relational terms
Note the terms: إسناد (attribution), مسند (predicate), مسند إليه (subject). Understand that the definition hinges on these terms. The subject is what the judgment is about, the predicate is what is attributed or negated.
These terms are borrowed from Arabic grammar but have precise logical meanings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرح القضية الحملية وأقسامها: من البيان السابق للقضايا نستطيع أن نستخلص تعريفاً للقضية الحملية فنقول: هي التي يكون الحكم فيها قائماً على إسناد شيءٍ إلى شيءٍ آخر أو نفيه عنه. أو هي التي يحكم فيها بعلاقة موجبة أو سالبة بين مُسند ومسندٍ إليه.
Explanation of the categorical proposition and its divisions: From the previous statement on propositions, we can extract a definition of the categorical proposition and say: It is that in which the judgment is based on attributing something to something else or negating it from it. Or it is that in which judgment is made with a positive or negative relation between a subject and a predicate.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage defines the categorical proposition (القضية الحملية). The author begins by stating that from the earlier discussion on propositions, we can derive a definition. Two equivalent formulations are given: first, a categorical proposition is one where the judgment is an attribution (إسناد) of one thing to another, or its negation; second, it is a judgment of a positive or negative relation between subject (مسند إليه) and predicate (مسند). This definition emphasizes that a categorical proposition does not involve a conditional connection to another proposition; it is a simple assertion or denial.

Key Terms
قضية حملية
إسناد
مسند
مسند إليه

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) A relation of causality

Key Takeaway
A categorical proposition is a judgment that directly attributes or negates a predicate to a subject, without any conditional connection.

The Seventh Type of Predication: Whole and Part
Defines the seventh type where one term is the whole and the other a part, with rules for partial predication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish valid partial predications from invalid total predications between a whole and its part, and identify metaphorical exceptions.

Core Idea
You can predicate a part of the whole partially, but never totally.

In Islamic logic, conceptual singulars can relate as whole and part, but not all predications are allowed. This lesson explains the three rules: you can predicate some of the whole on the part, or the part on some of the whole, but you cannot predicate the whole on the part or vice versa in a total or absolute manner. However, metaphorical usage is permitted for rhetorical emphasis, as in the prophetic hadith 'Al-Hajj Arafah.'

Guided Path
1
Identify the whole and the part
Given two terms, determine which one is the whole (al-kull) and which is the part (al-juz'). For example, 'face' is the whole, 'eyes' is a part.
2
Check the type of predication
If the predication is partial (using 'some of' or 'part of'), it is allowed. If it is total (e.g., 'A is B' without qualification), it is forbidden.
Total predication is also called haml kulli; absolute predication (haml mutlaq) is also forbidden.
3
Recognize metaphorical exceptions
If a total predication appears in religious texts, it may be metaphorical for rhetorical purposes, as in 'Al-Hajj Arafah.' The whole is used for an essential part.
Metaphor is not a logical predication but a rhetorical device.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سابعاً: إذا كان أحد المفردين التصوريين كلاً وكان الآخر جزءاً له فالحمل بينهما يكون على الوجه التالي: أ ـ يحمل بعض الكل على الجزء فيقال: العينان بعض الوجه أو من الوجه. ب ـ ويحمل الجزء على بعض الكل، فيقال: بعض الوجه عينان. جـ ـ ولا يحمل أي واحد منهما على الآخر حملاً كلياً ولا حملاً مطلقاً، فلا يقال: العينان وجه، ولا: الوجه عينان. لأن الكل في هذه الحالة مباين لجزئه، ولا ينطبق أي واحد منهما على ما صدق الآخر. وما يستعمل من ذلك عند الناس فهو من قبيل المجاز لغرض بلاغي، ومنه قول الرسول ﷺ: «الحج عرفة».
Seventhly: If one of the two conceptual singulars is a whole and the other is a part of it, then the predication between them is as follows: (a) Some of the whole is predicated upon the part, so it is said: 'The two eyes are part of the face' or 'from the face.' (b) And the part is predicated upon some of the whole, so it is said: 'Some of the face is two eyes.' (c) And neither one of them is predicated upon the other with total predication nor with absolute predication, so it is not said: 'The two eyes are a face,' nor 'The face is two eyes,' because the whole in this case is distinct from its part, and neither applies to what the other is true of. And what is used among people of that kind is by way of metaphor for a rhetorical purpose, including the saying of the Prophet ﷺ: 'The pilgrimage is Arafat.'
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage defines the seventh type of relation between two conceptual singulars: one is the whole and the other a part. The author lists three rules. First, a part of the whole can be predicated of the part itself, e.g., 'The eyes are part of the face' — here 'part of the face' (some of the whole) is predicated of 'the eyes' (a part). Second, the part can be predicated of some of the whole, e.g., 'Some of the face is eyes.' Third, total or absolute predication is forbidden: you cannot say 'The eyes are a face' (whole) or 'The face is eyes' (whole). The reason is that the whole is distinct from its part in essence and extension; they do not coincide. However, metaphorical use is allowed for rhetorical emphasis, such as the prophetic saying 'Al-Hajj 'Arafah' — meaning that the essential part of the pilgrimage is the standing at Arafat, not that the pilgrimage is literally only Arafat.

Key Terms
كل (kull): The whole entity that comprises parts; here used for a term that denotes a whole as opposed to its part. [Note: In logic, 'kull' can also refer to universal quantifier; here it means the whole object.]
جزء (juz'): A part of the whole, i.e., a constituent element.
حمل كلي (haml kulli): Total predication, where the predicate applies to every instance of the subject; here forbidden when the two terms are whole and part. [Note: In other contexts, 'haml kulli' may mean universal predication as opposed to partial; here it specifically means 'the whole is predicated of the part'.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following predications is NOT allowed according to the seventh type?
A) العينان بعض الوجه (al-'aynani ba'd al-wajh)
B) بعض الوجه عينان (ba'd al-wajh 'aynani)
C) العينان وجه (al-'aynani wajh)
D) بعض الوجه ليس عينين (ba'd al-wajh laysa 'aynayn)

Key Takeaway
A whole and its part cannot be predicated of each other entirely; only partial predication is logically valid unless used metaphorically.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Given the terms 'الصلاة' (salah) as the whole and 'الركوع' (ruku') as a part, determine which of the following predications are valid: (i) الركوع بعض الصلاة (ruku' is part of salah), (ii) الصلاة ركوع (salah is ruku'), (iii) بعض الصلاة ركوع (some of salah is ruku'). Explain each using the rules.
